## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, a fundamental constitutive relation in materials science. Temperature typically modifies elastic modulus and introduces thermal softening or thermally-activated deformation mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law with temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain for plastic deformation)
- Ramberg-Osgood (inverted form): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * epsilon**c3) (elastoplastic stress-strain)
- Johnson-Cook strength model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T)**c4 (flow stress with strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 - c1 * T**c2) (linear elasticity with power-law thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturating hardening behavior)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * exp(c3 * T) (saturating hardening with exponential thermal effect)
- Hollomon equation with temperature: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (power-law hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal dependence)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic or rubber-like behavior)
- Neo-Hookean type: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * epsilon**3) * (1 + c2 * T) (hyperelastic with temperature dependence)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (power-law with pre-strain offset)
- Exponential softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (elastic modulus with exponential temperature dependence)
- Bilinear with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**2 * (1 + c3 * T) (quadratic stress-strain with temperature coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening in metals → multiplicative factor (1 - (T/Tm)^c) or exp(-c*T) reducing stress at higher temperatures
- Strain hardening saturation → terms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) that plateau at large strains
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 for work-hardening metals (Hollomon/Ludwik behavior)
- Yield stress offset → additive constant c0 + f(epsilon) separating elastic limit from hardening contribution
- Temperature-modulus coupling → elastic modulus as E(T) = c0*(1 + c1*T) or c0*exp(c1*T), appearing as prefactor to strain terms
- Rubber elasticity / hyperelastic → odd polynomial in strain (epsilon - c*epsilon**3) from entropic elasticity
- Creep/viscoplastic regime → Arrhenius-type temperature activation exp(c/T) combined with power-law strain rate or strain
- Separable temperature-strain structure → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), where stress factorizes into independent strain and temperature functions

We can't have both T and T*epsilon**3 from this candidate.
